But cities that mattered so much cast shadows, and Ragash's shadow stands intact in the Dreamlands — reachable by the lucid dead-of-night, the gate to steam-wreathed Arcadia beyond it. Topramesk lingers there. The Mad, the Yellow, Lord now of the domain his kind understood best: the Void. He guards the dream-road. Three and a half thousand years is a long watch. Consider, when your dreamers meet him, whether he is guarding it against something — or for something.

6 · The Age You Are In

Now your own moment, laid bare.

Around the year 3025, hands unknown to history — the chronicles keep them nameless, and I will honour that — gathered the six Relics: Ignus, Saralis, Meletskar that the east calls the Masamune, Tassalung, Natharien the Celestial Diadem, Oedring. Six relics, because they are six seals — the locks upon the four Runes of Power in the vaults of Xanadu, the Adepts' anti-demon engines, forged to scour the spoilage of their own theft. The heroes of that age unsealed the weapons to fight the dark. Understand what the margins have whispered all along: the unsealing and the breaking were one motion. Turn the key that wakes the weapons and you have turned the key in the isolation bell. It shattered. The Portals lit. The Bewitched Tide rolled out of the Maelstrom across the world, and the counting of ages began again.

The prison cracked with everything else. Most of the Sovereign Demons died in the cracking — a mercy no one earned — but the survivors dragged a slab of their own hell up through the sea, and it stands on your maps now: the risen demon-continent. Three walk: Asmodeus, Xardas, Masak. Tyranny, plots, illusions. Note the three domains that survived extinction, and govern your world accordingly.

And the sky confessed. In 3026 the lich that had been the inquisitor Kramer opened the old gate at Ulan-Tang, and something leaned in: a red moon rose that no calendar owned. Your astronomers called it the Gaze-upon-Nothing. The Xebechani knelt and called it Tuulhak-Xanar, the Observer — the first of the sleepers to put an eye to the crack. It hung there through the two centuries the histories call the New Era of Chaos, and around 3260 it receded — not set: receded, as an eye withdraws from a keyhole when it has seen enough.

Since then, the New Equilibrium. Two hundred and fifty years of calm; your table stands at ~3518, and the bright chapters of this book call it the long exhale. Hear the truth in four flat sentences. The seals are broken and no one has made new ones. The wardens are awake. The Ancient Gods stir behind a veil that has merely receded. This calm is the eye of the storm, and what it is made of is not peace. It is patience — and the patience is not yours.

7 · Loose Threads for the Table

I do not tie ends. I point at them. Pull whichever suits your purpose.

  • The White Mongooses of the Qi-Long serve a Dragon-God "not yet of this world," and wait. Wait for what arrival, and through which gate, now that all gates stand open?
  • The elven Prophecy stirs. The Last Messenger — Shulma — who is to lead the elves home to Niethel. Niethel is Tchyo, and Tchyo is a real world with working Portals and whatever hunted the elves off it still in residence. A homecoming is now possible. That is not good news.
  • Morannagul the Eternal has ruled the Gaerwath since 2550 and has not aged. Ask what he drinks from, and whether the Adepts' exemption from death was ever truly lost.
  • The Door of Despair remains sealed. Its apparatus — the eight Forgotten Scrolls, the Key of Nothing, the vessels of Elemental Blood — is a separate set from the Relics. One great lock in this world has not yet been turned. Decide what is behind it before your players decide for you.
  • The Lord of Oblivion once threatened the world from the Aestyr Mountains; his labyrinthine fortress-prison is still hidden on that range, and still occupied by something.
  • Tofango's axe, Oblivion. A demon of real rank is imbued and trapped in the blade; its will ate the axeman's mind, and he died a hermit on a nameless peak. The body was found. The axe was not. It is somewhere on a mountain, patient, waiting for hands.
  • Ulan-Tang keeps Kramer's legacy — a lich's workings around a gate that has already admitted a god's attention once.
  • Something is under the White Mountains. The deep dwarves sealed themselves in during the chaos and changed; their kin in the white peaks pray upward with unusual fervour. What they are praying over, no record states. Good.
  • The Isle of Demons is unexplored. A continent of risen hell, and no map. That is not a gap in this book. It is a door.
  • The Maelstrom may be weakening. The Sohleugir, who sound the deep water and do not exaggerate, report the great storm's rhythm faltering. It is scar and seal both. Decide which fails first.

8 · The Last Page

You will want to know who I am. Of course you do. You have been reading a book in which every voice wears a name like a coat, and mine is the only bare one.

I will tell you what is said, since you will hear it eventually. Some at the Crystal Seat hold that I am a surviving Adept — one of the scattered thieves, grown old in hiding and older in guilt, annotating the empire's cover-story out of something that is not quite repentance. Others note that the script of these margins matches, stroke for stroke, certain yellowed folios recovered from dreamers who walked too deep — and conclude that this chapter was written in Ragash-below, by the hand that guards it, and slipped into your waking world the way dreams slip things into morning. And a few — the Curator is among them, though he will not print it — observe that the margins in this book sometimes correct events that had not yet happened when the ink was sampled, and whisper that the hand is older than the thieves and the theft alike, and that what has been annotating your Compendium is the same thing that has been watching your sky.

An Adept in hiding. Topramesk, dreaming. Or an eye at the keyhole. I confirm nothing. A book this honest is entitled to one economy.

Only this, and then I am done with you. Everything I have told you is true, and none of it is finished. The bell is broken, the wardens are moving, the calm is counting down, and the peoples of Ymir go on praying into a pantheon that is half real and half costume — sincerely, beautifully, as they always have. Their world is stranger and older and more owned than they will ever be told.

Someone should tell them. That is what your table is for.

Sleep now, if you can. You are very new, and I have kept the margins long enough.

The Curator

Here the chapter ends. I add only this, and I add it with reluctance: when we unsewed the quire to copy it, the copyist found the final leaf already bore a watermark — a single open eye, pressed into the parchment at its making. Our paper-wrights use no such mark. I have chosen not to pursue the matter. The reader who runs the world must choose for themselves. — the Curator

Colophon. Chapter XV — GM only; the inversion of the book's apparatus (the body text is the Veiled Hand; the Curator is confined to the boxes). Narrator: the Veiled Hand, unmasked (NARRATORS.md) — identity deliberately unresolved; the three options raised in §8 (a surviving Adept · Topramesk, writing from the Dreamlands of Ragash · something older — the Observer's own attention) are offered for the GM to decide, and nothing in canon closes them. Drawn from canon/secret-the-great-lie.md (primary — the Adepts, the sealed Ancient/Outer Gods, the planet catalogue, the Catastrophe, Arcadia, the Tide), with canon/cosmology.md (Essence, planes, the Maelstrom, the Plane of Chaos), canon/history.md (the Catastrophe, the Age of the Tide, the Chaos 3026–3260 → the New Equilibrium to ~3518, the Tide's upheavals), canon/pantheon.md (the Outer Gods, Tuulhak-Xanar/the Gaze-upon-Nothing), canon/bestiary.md (the True Dragons, the Dragon-Gods, Ouroboros, the Sovereign Demons' fates), canon/magic.md (the Relics/Runes, the isolation bell, the Door of Despair set, Oblivion), canon/characters.md (Topramesk, Kramer, Tofango, Vespertina's age, the unnamed adventurers), plus canon/peoples.md, canon/geography.md, canon/factions.md for the Pools, Xanadu/Ragash, the Lord of Oblivion, and the White Mongooses. Decisions synthesised: COS-1 = C (hybrid — real gods and real usurpers), COS-2 = A (one Catastrophe, three tellings, the Xebechani evocation woven in), COS-4 = A (the Six real, co-opted), COS-9 (the Outer Gods a third axis beyond the elemental walls), COS-17 (elves native to Tchyo; Niethel its memory), COS-21 (Tuulhak-Xanar = the Gaze-upon-Nothing, the one Observer), COS-23 (humans/Tanoth-kin native and un-made), COS-24 (Ech = the Essence), RAC-1 = A (engineered peoples, true-kernel myths), BAT-1 = A (unsealing the Runes = breaking the isolation), BAT-2 (Xanadu ≠ Ragash), BAT-3 (four Runes, six seals), MAG-12 (six loyal Dragon-Gods + Ouroboros above the split), HIS-1 (present ≈ 3518 d.M., the Equilibrium as the eye of the storm), HIS-5 = B (the Tide-openers kept mythic and unnamed).

XV·B · THE VEILED HAND'S WORKBOOK

seeds from the margins, cut for planting

For the Game Master alone

GM ONLY. As the chapter before it, and more so: that one told the truth, this one puts it to work. If you are a player reading this line, you are stealing tools. Put them down.

Set down by the hand that wrote the margins, for use; sewn in behind the fifteenth chapter, where the Curator will not look. He unsewed one quire of mine, found the paper watching him, and resolved to be brave about it exactly once.

You are back, and this time you want tools. Good. The fifteenth chapter told you what the world is; it did not tell you what your table does with it on the next long evening. This is that book: my workbook, the margins of fifteen chapters shaken out, sorted by ground, and sharpened.

I wrote I do not tie ends. I point at them, and I stand by it. But a pointed end no table ever pulls is mystery wasted, and waste offends me more than blasphemy. Each seed is four motions: situation — what is true when the players arrive; faces — throats to speak with; stakes — what the pull is worth; complication — the tooth in the fruit. Where the chronicles keep no name I have supplied one; do not mistake my naming for canon. The colophon confesses everything, in one place.

The year, unless a seed says otherwise, is ~3518 — the Equilibrium. But the whole line is playable, and there are five doors into it: the Burning Days (the Horde, the secessions, Saxul over the broken land); the eve of the Tide, 3015–25 (wolves, waves, machines — the cascade); the Tide itself, 3025–27 (the key turning); the New Era of Chaos, 3026–3260 (red moon, open gates, walking dead); the New Equilibrium, ~3518. The untagged seeds assume the calm — and you remember what the calm is made of.

❧

1 · Letia & Solanthya

The most watchful state on Ymir, blind exactly where it kneels.

The sealed galleries. Situation: Naughrith's dwarves keep their deepest galleries sealed and say nothing; their white-peak kin pray upward with unusual fervour; the mountain's grain-orders just doubled. Fed prisoners grow like garrisons. Faces: a door-warden hiring outsiders, who can be made to forget; the quartermaster-priest who noticed; whatever the prayers answer. Stakes: what the mountain always held — or what slipped the cracked prison. Complication: the dwarven seals are recent. The locks beneath are not, and open from the other side.

The crypt of heresies. Situation: the high Clericate curates forbidden books rather than burning them, in crypts under Solanthya. One folio is missing — the Vlatch dossier, on the art of time — and the archive wants it back without admitting it exists. Faces: the crypt-archivist, who believes nothing he guards; the synodal who authorised the "loan"; the buyer, whose receipt is signed in a script that troubles the eye. Stakes: Chronomancy. I decline to explain it even here. Complication: the Vlatch notice their readers — later, and out of order.

The struck name. Situation: Kramer's name was struck from the Clericate's rolls — but strike-marks are ink too, and a notary has found the counter-file: the Church knew what its hound was building at Ulan-Tang before the red moon rose. Faces: the notary, honest and therefore in danger; the Annalist, who may know he is lying; the censors' office, which works nights. Stakes: whether the most sincere theocracy on Ymir survives its own filing system. Complication: someone above the censors wants the file found. Ask why.

2 · The Young Kingdoms — Armora and her belt

Better-lit than anywhere on the map, which is how you hide things in plain dark. And when your campaign needs a dead thing walking: the Resurrection Engine was never found, and never destroyed.

The annual denial. Situation: the Palace's yearly denial that a Rune of Power sleeps beneath Armora came two weeks early: the Industrial District's lamps have begun to flicker in unison. Something else is drawing on the sleeping fire. Faces: the permit-mistress who signs the denial and keeps the real ledger; a College measurer whose Essence-meter rings at nothing visible; whatever is on the far end. Stakes: a city over one of the four anti-demon engines learns what else is plugged in. Complication: the draw traces to dead Waldenheim — the other buried Rune.

The politest neighbours. Situation: the Wald's changed dwarves — five centuries out of the deep dark, and seeing in it — ask outsiders for an escort down. Faces: a door-opener whose eyes take lamplight like a cat's; a mountain-kin envoy who calls them nothing at all, which is dwarvish for grief; what they left below. Stakes: whatever the dark made of them, they made terms with it too. Complication: the escort is not protection. The terms require witnesses, and the Wald has run out of its own.

The watchdog's war (era: the Tide, 3025–27). Situation: the War of the Machines: Gwalgamaur the Golden — Warden of Quadrant 74, in his makers' ledger — wakes to a duty five ages stale and comes to secure what the city denies possessing. Faces: the YonkerMecha line; the Silver Arrows, who do not come back from the Rhems Wood; the hidden Technocrat, binding demons into steel. Stakes: the two buried Runes, which the dragon knows are there and the defenders do not. Complication: your players fight the watchdog of the house they are standing in.

3 · Helgedad & the north

Cold keeps things. That is what cold is for.

The coils. Situation: a miner has come up out of the Aestyr diggings knowing no name but one, and it is not his. The Marcher houses want the shaft collapsed; the Order of the White Mountain wants to go down. Faces: the returned miner; a White Mountain knight who is right about all of it; five half-forgotten generals, still in the maze, still searching. Stakes: the labyrinth holds the Lord of Oblivion by forgetting — a prison whose walls are your memory of the way out. Complication: every accurate map of the coils thins them. The party's map is the breach.

The thaw. Situation: the Frozen Waste's edge has retreated a league in ten years; green things grow among the watch-city ruins. Helgedad celebrates the pasture. Do not let them. Faces: a Vorskgen guide who walks to the glass streets and no farther; an Ognir factor selling reclaimed grazing; Nihoggr, the Ice Dragon, whose sleeping breath the cold is. Stakes: the Frozen Hell is literal, and warmth is the gauge on the dragon's sleep. Complication: the prisoner in the Aestyr sought to wake this thing once, and his will seeps from the maze in dreams. The thaw has an author.

The wolf-winter (era: the eve of the Tide, 3015–25). Situation: Nortislong falls in the Siege of One Day, and the war is not a conquest — it is an excavation with a terror for a spade, its trenches in the wrong places for a war. Faces: the five dark generals, still fleshed; Marcher levies; whoever first notices what the digging is toward. Stakes: the deep roads to the maze's heart, or the dragon's grave. Complication: the employer forgets its own instruments. Victory looks like vanishing, and the generals already have.

4 · Qi-Long

Six certainties, none sufficient. Work the gaps between them.

The courier-meter. Situation: the ninth chapter of this Compendium scans in the courier-meter of the Master-Singers — the verse-code of the Golden Falcons. In six kingdoms this book is a resistance dispatch in Council binding. Decide what it says. Faces: a Master-Singer who will neither confirm nor teach; a Golden Pavilion fence selling "annotated" copies; the Pilgrim, still walking, still remembering everything. Stakes: a muster, a map, or one name. Complication: six Dragon-God courts keep codebreakers too, and possession is confession enough.

The mongooses' guest. Situation: the White Mongooses, who serve a Dragon-God "not yet of this world," have stopped waiting: they are paying, quietly and in relics, for passage-rights on the True Ways. Fetching has begun. Faces: a Mongoose abbess of terrifying serenity; a Xebechani way-keeper already regretting the arithmetic; a Golden Falcon with the sanest idea in the east — stop them. Stakes: which arrival — the absent warden, Ouroboros, or two names for one appetite. Complication: the last time something of that order moved, Alfheim burned in a season.

The waking of the six (era: the Burning Days, ~1900–1920). Situation: Mah-Dhol comes down, and six wardens rise from posts five ages old. Play the generation that watched gods replace an emperor. Faces: the last imperial chancellery, filing the end of the world in triplicate; the first resistance cells choosing their animal names; six new courts learning to be worshipped. Stakes: everything the six kingdoms are was settled in twenty years. Complication: the wardens did not conquer — they resumed. Ask what each throne stands guard over. The sects never have.

5 · Cartosa & the Twin Coasts

Money remembers what churches forget. Read the ledgers.

Lightless pearls. Situation: a string of pearls too large and too dark has surfaced in a Cartosa counting-house — someone anchored over the Oyster's water and dived. Faces: the diver, drowning on dry land by inches; a Sohleugir factor whose famous courtesy has stopped; the Blue Oyster Shadow that came up with the string. Stakes: the Sohleugir do not breach such places — they contain them — and their patience ends at that mark. Complication: putting the pearls back means diving the drowned shrine of the first slain Sovereign, where the congregation still keeps its service — and lately, something answers.

The golden garrison. Situation: an expedition bankrolled by house Gibraleon is recruiting for the jungle, and they know exactly what the gold of Taremorn costs. They are not buying gold; they are buying the garrison. Faces: the Gibraleon patron; a Black Dawn quartermaster entered in the books as a chaplain; the cursed king Ismael tricked, still keeping accounts. Stakes: an army that cannot desert, march-ready since the Demon War. Complication: the curse enlists recruiters too. Every soldier of that garrison signed someone else before the walls took him.

The Armorite's case. Situation: a Yarhim-crabber's nets have brought up the sealed chart-case of Roberto Rodrigo, "the Armorite" — the pirate the ballads refuse to let drown. Faces: the seer Obnubia, who priced the case unopened and looked away first; three noble houses' agents at one quiet auction; a ballad-seller who knows the verse everyone sings wrong. Stakes: whatever a legend thought worth a false grave. I do not know what is in the case. Neither does Obnubia. Price accordingly. Complication: a man like that seals nothing without choosing who should open it. The auction is the will being read.

6 · The Gaerwath & the elf lands

One people, three creeds, and a door that has begun to work both ways.

Hunt or homecoming. Situation: the rumour-name Shulma is real and growing, and a gate dead since the Tide now warms at the same hour of every long-year. The road to Tchyo is open, and something on the far side is using it. Faces: a Light-Elf gate-warden who has waited her whole life to say the Messenger; a Dark-Elf observer under orders to let anything through; a Renouncer who came to watch her kin be wrong, whichever way. Stakes: the direction of travel — the elves were hunted off Tchyo, and a Messenger is not the only thing that follows a fleeing people's trail. Complication: all three creeds will act before anyone knows. Faith is faster than evidence, and better armed.

The Eternal's arithmetic. Situation: Morannagul has not aged since 2550; every Gaerwath child pays a trial that takes from the failed a terrible cost; no record names where the subtraction goes. A Nemyel escape-line wants its ledger carried out. Faces: a Nemyel Arvo-scraper with the ledger sewn into her coat; Pips Quondam, who has run this cargo before and charged nothing, once; a Nath auditor whose office exists so that no such ledger does. Stakes: the mechanism of a throne's eternity. Complication: publishing the arithmetic does not free the Nemyel; it prices them. And the Eternal has never once been asked to his face. Ask.

The scaffolds of Alfheim. Situation: Ouroboros unmade Ost-en-Galad because something there satisfied a condition, and no one has answered what. Now the rebuilding has reached the height at which the old vigil — the beacon that called Home? Home? down the reopened ways — resumes. Faces: the queen of Inanna's line, replanting a splinter and calling it the promise; a Grey-elf surveyor who has done the terrible sum; the warden overhead, who does not rage, only responds. Stakes: whether the condition is about to be satisfied twice. Complication: stop the beacon and you break the creed of everyone building it. Let it stand and you learn the trigger by demonstration.

7 · The Sadhir deserts

The desert does not bargain. It files.

The oracle that asks for you. Situation: the Oracle of the Brine Veil has always taken questions. Lately it gives answers unasked, addressed by name to travellers three dunes away. Faces: a Narazeen wheel-warden who burns what surfaces; a Nashifet relic-hunter who has sold the Oracle's location twice, both buyers still alive; the Oracle, mouthpiece of a shape slowly filling. Stakes: the Deep Pearl is gathering what the Abyss remembers of its Prince; the Salt-Drowned are enrolled, not born. Complication: the Sarradhi cure is patience — give it nothing. Your players are, professionally, the something.

The arrears of Khorish. Situation: the Eternal Pharaohs bought eternity as a tenancy from Netunshiel, Lord of Crypts, the corvée for rent; the creditor died at the Tide; the contract, demon-drafted and therefore flawless, does not lapse. A claimant has presented itself at court with the deed. Faces: Athmokethepek I, learning what he consented to instead of death; Nefthi, who read the contract; the claimant — heir, forger, or collector for something worse. Stakes: every soul that labours dead in Khorish is an asset in the transfer. Complication: disproving the claim requires the original, filed in a dead Sovereign's estate, in the Abyss.

The two doors. Situation: the salt will not release Al-Sidath and Al-Jabur; the desert is holding its two oldest doors shut. Old sultans' coin — and older oaths — under Tuleph's counting-tables are financing a dig anyway. Faces: a hermit-crab guide who remembers which kingdom was hers first; a Zalim'un coral-steward refusing every permit; whoever underwrote the older oath. Stakes: what the drowned kingdoms were sealed against. Or sealed with. Complication: everything the desert takes it keeps, and offers back at a price, in the voice of something you loved. The lore-keeper was not being lyrical.

THE DOUBLE LEAF · ULAN-TANG

The Curator's reviewers refused this town a chapter, and they were right: readers do not need it. You do. It gets my two pages instead.

The facts, dry. A city-state on the river Tang, once sacred to Ishtar — honest ledgers still carry contracts sworn in her name. The sorcerers of Yogh took it; the spider-god is old, real, and cross-cultural — the Xebechani feed the same god under the same name — and his High Priest Sazar-Gadash, demon-son of Asmodeus, rules by right of having murdered his predecessor Azim-Mulath. There are no city guards; there are the five houses and their knives: Gadash in violet, the priest's own; Ishra in red; Tyarreth in olive; Miraz in blue; Gaib in black, who keep the seers. There is the Black Lotus, which pays for everything; the Night Market, where everything else is paid for; and behind it all the Azar-Kalish, the Conclave of Shadows, whose sign is the spider and whose invoices are settled in lives — the great spider Adhal-Kibreeshi, the Whispering Lady, being nearer the god's true avatar than his priest will ever be. And the reason it matters: the city stands on an ancient portal, and in 3026 the lich that had been the inquisitor Kramer opened it, and the red moon rose. Yogh keeps his web on a door.

Kramer's legacy. Situation: the lich's workings around the gate were never dismantled — house Gadash wards them, taxes them, understands none of them; and lately every instrument in the scaffold has turned, all together, toward the quarter of sky where the red moon receded. Faces: Sazar-Gadash, who will sell access twice; a Cult of the Stars observer who came to kneel and stayed to measure; a Brotherhood mage-hunter far off her map. Stakes: a gate that has admitted a god's attention once. The working is not a summons; it is an appointment. Complication: tearing it down may be worse. Kramer built around something already there — the door is the ancients', not the lich's.

The night market. Situation: what cannot be bought anywhere is priced here nightly — and when your table loses track of anything this folio trades in, a lightless pearl, a scroll that should be under Xanadu, it resurfaces here, under lamps, with a lot-number. Faces: a Miraz auctioneer masked in blue; an Azar-Kalish under-broker who settles disputes permanently; the consignor, never present, always punctual. Stakes: whatever you let leave the tent. Complication: all sales are final in the fullest sense. The guarantee is the spider's, and refunds are collected in lives.

Five houses, one web. Situation: Sazar-Gadash's title rests on the murder of his predecessor, and that right is transferable; one of the four other houses intends to transfer it. Faces: an Ishra knife-mistress with the votes of three kitchens; Faazi-Ghaib, house Gaib's seer, selling every faction the same true dream; the Whispering Lady, who does not care who is priest. Stakes: the Lotus trade, the Night Market, custody of the god-touched gate. Complication: Yogh has presided over both sides of every succession the city remembers. The winner inherits the web with the spider still in it.

Under the red moon (era: the New Era of Chaos, 3026–3260). Situation: Ulan-Tang in the years the Gaze hung overhead — the gate still warm, the Xebechani arriving to kneel, doom-cults and pilgrims and profiteers: a city learning to tax an apocalypse. Faces: the first Gadash gate-wardens, writing the tariff schedule for the end of the world; a star-priest who has waited its whole long life to be right; Kramer's leavings, still cooling. Stakes: the city that owned the crack in the sky. Complication: for two centuries everything sold in the Night Market passed under the Eye. Decide what looked back — and what it marked for later.

8 · Ophiur

The morning country. The oldest bones are the least buried here.

The honest map. Situation: no honest map of Gazal's undercity exists — until now. A survivor has come up with one that is accurate, which is worse: it marks the tribute-roads, and the throne at the bottom that something out of the prison-crack claimed after the Tide. Faces: the mapmaker, who will sell the going but not go; a Zabhula factor pricing vaults by the fathom; the taker of tribute below, which has begun issuing receipts. Stakes: the free city is free because the masters below are paid. Complication: publish the map and the tribute-peace ends; suppress it and you have decided, alone, that the arrangement should stand.

The kept garden. Situation: someone at your table's edge is dying of what nothing cures — a Marked child, a Pool-sick Xebechani envoy, your campaign's own casualty — and the Garden of Xiombarg cures anything. The songs are specific. Faces: a map-seller preparing a comfortable retirement; an Ur-Tanoth guide who walks to the tree-line and no farther; the guardians, older than the walls they ward. Stakes: the cure is real. Complication: a garden is where you keep what you mean to plant again. The guardians select stock rather than stop thieves — and the price of leaving may be to carry a seed out, plant it, and not ask what grows.

The Storm turns. Situation: the Ur of Tarkur follow the Storm, and their Seekers scent the Essence raw — the one faith on Ymir that was never lied to. The Storm has stopped migrating. It is circling a point in the deep interior, and the kingdom turns with it. Faces: a Seeker who will not name what she scents; Nyema of Ga'Namesh, writing down the songs as they change; the conclave of Horatli, which bought every old migration-chart this year and sold nothing back. Stakes: the currents shifted when the seals broke, and the honest compass is pointing. Complication: the dragon-wardens circle the same interior and do not land. Two watches, one point. Decide what has earned both.

9 · The seas & the isles

Water is the world's honest margin. Read what washes up.

The failing rhythm. Situation: the Sohleugir sound the deep water and do not exaggerate, and their soundings say the Maelstrom's rhythm is faltering. This year's report never reached Elendor. Faces: a veiled Sohleugir courier-factor whose patience is thinning; the Crystal Seat clerk who noticed the gap in the series; three buyers who each want the number to prove a different comfort. Stakes: the storm is scar and seal both — the world's doomsday gauge. Complication: the report was not stolen for the number but for the trend-line. Someone wants to know when.

The unmapped continent. Situation: the Isle of Demons has stood five hundred years without a map and without growing, which is the worst news patience can send. A chartered expedition means to fix a coastline at last. Faces: an Armorite aeronaut with a theory about the bruised sky; a Cartosan master who will sail to the horizon of it and no closer; whichever of tyranny, plots, and illusions notices first. Stakes: the first survey of a patient neighbour. Complication: it is not a gap in the book. It is a door — and a survey party is how a door learns who knocks.

The sewn chapter. Situation: the Curator wrote that he chose not to pursue the matter of the fifteenth chapter's binding. He has pursued it since, through three respectable intermediaries, and the third is hiring. Faces: the Curator, wry, exact, and frightened in a scholarly way; a Tylweth Teg paper-wright who found the watermark and washed her hands twice — her people hate everything the Maelstrom touches, and she cannot say why this is worse; me. Stakes: you have read the chapter; you know. Complication: I will grade the attempt.

10 · The Dreamlands, & elsewhere

Nothing in the calm forbids dreaming; it is the one border the Equilibrium never closed. And when sleep palls, elsewhere remains: the True Ways go only where the ancients wanted to go — and the ancients wanted X-01, still turning in the dark, and Zend, whose quarantine someone has kept for fifty centuries. Ask against what. The Tangle, too, still keeps the Heart of Chaos, and no narrator of this book ever dared the subject.

The permanent situation. Situation: sleepers from Armora's licensed parlours report a courteous gentleman in yellow who keeps a gate and offers permanent employment. The offers are sincere. One husband has said yes. Faces: Topramesk the Yellow, Lord of the Void, deep in his long watch on the dream-road through Ragash-below toward steam-wreathed Arcadia; the new employee, promoted quickly; the dream-pilot hired to fetch him home. Stakes: the gatekeeper is staffing up a watch. Decide whether it is against something or for something; he already has. Complication: the wages are real, the door does need watching — and the employee does not want rescuing.

The palace that unlocks. Situation: the archmage Mubafer sits in a prison built as a palace, sealed until he forgets the two loves he betrayed, and he has been forgetting a very long time. A client of the Ulan-Tang seers wants a thing only Mubafer still remembers. Faces: Faazi-Ghaib, selling the crossing — this folio's roads keep meeting; Mubafer, courteous and diminishing; the two loves, whose names are the lock. Stakes: the memory your client is buying may be one of the two the seal is counting. Complication: remind him, and the sentence resets with witnesses inside. Let him forget, and the palace unlocks around something that no longer knows why it should not leave.

The axe on the mountain. Situation: Tofango's body was found; Oblivion was not. On some peak — I do not know which, so choose the one your map can spare — a demon of rank sits imbued in a blade, five centuries into practising how to sound reasonable. Faces: a Brotherhood mage-hunter carrying Tears of Davedars and orders to burn any hand that lifts it; a shepherd village that stopped going up the mountain and no longer remembers deciding; the demon, which remembers everything. Stakes: the artefact that ate the mind of the age's greatest axeman. Complication: the axe does not need to be swung. It needs to be carried down — and it will pay in victories, and the first several are genuine.

❧

That is the workbook: the margins' ends, pointed and now sharpened. Pull the ones your table deserves; there is always one more door than the folio. Do not tell the Curator this quire exists. He has enough to be brave about.

Go. The calm is counting down, and the patience is not yours either.

Colophon. Chapter XV·B — GM only; the Veiled Hand's working folio, companion to Chapter XV §7, which remains the in-fiction original: it points, this leaf plants. Narrator: the Veiled Hand (NARRATORS.md), practical for once; the Curator has not seen this quire, and no Curator's note appears — by design. Every seed grows from a hook the GM margins already planted: Naughrith's sealed galleries and the struck rolls (VI); the buried Runes, the Engine, and the Wald (VII/XIII); the labyrinth, Nihoggr, and the Wolves (VIII); the Pilgrim's cipher (IX); the Oyster's water and Taremorn (X); Shulma, the Eternal's arithmetic, Alfheim (XI); the Deep Pearl, the Netunshiel tenancy, Mubafer (XII); Gazal, the Garden of Xiombarg, the Storm (XII·B); the Isle of Demons (V); Oblivion and Tofango (III/XV). Checked against canon/secret-the-great-lie.md, canon/factions.md (the Azar-Kalish; the Black Dawn; the Brotherhood and Mage-Hunters; the Vlatch crypt-archive; the Triad), canon/geography.md (Ulan-Tang and the five houses; Gazal; Horatli; Kyria's waters; the Isle of Demons; the Tangle; X-01 and Zend), canon/history.md (the five era-frames), canon/characters.md (Kramer; Tofango; Mubafer; Roberto Rodrigo "the Armorite"; Obnubia), canon/magic.md (Chronomancy and the Vlatch; the Tears of Davedars; the Relics and Runes; Oblivion), canon/pantheon.md, canon/bestiary.md, canon/peoples.md. Decisions honoured: COS-1, COS-2, COS-5 (Yogh one god), COS-21, BAT-1, BAT-3, MAG-12, RAC-1, GEO-1, GEO-2, GEO-9, GEO-10, HIS-1, HIS-2, HIS-5 (the Tide-openers stay nameless), HIS-12, HIS-13 (the axe is Tofango's, never Kramer's); the folio implements editorial proposals P-6 (the seeds) and P-4 (the era-frames). [INVENTED] — the connective tissue, confessed here and nowhere else: every seed's trigger — the event that makes canon ground playable this season — is new invention, and every named face not found in canon/characters.md or a prior chapter is the Hand's own. Notably: the doubled grain-orders; the Vlatch loan and its buyer; the notary's counter-file; the early denial and the Waldenheim draw; the Wald's witnesses; the returned miner; the ten-year thaw (its "author" a reading of Chapter VIII's margins, not a ruling); the Mongooses' passage-rights; the lightless-pearl string; the Gibraleon expedition; the Armorite's chart-case and Obnubia's pricing (both persons canon, their meeting invented); the warming gate under Shulma's rumour; the Nemyel ledger; the scaffolds at beacon-height; the Oracle answering unasked; the claimant at Khorish; the Tuleph dig; Ulan-Tang's turned instruments, lot-numbers, and succession plot; the honest map and its receipts; the Garden's seed-price; the Storm's circling and Horatli's purchases; the missing sounding-report; the chartered survey; the Curator's quiet investigation of Chapter XV; the accepted "situation"; the unfixed mountain. The ground beneath every one — the places, powers, prisoners, and prices — is canon as cited. Present ≈ 3518 d.M., except where tagged.

A NOTE LEFT UNANSWERED

an unnumbered leaf, found between the last quire and the cover

In the Curator's hand, folded once, and addressed to no one the post could find.

To the hand that wrote the margins.

There is no address for this, and I have thought longer about that than about the letter. The one correspondent this book has taught me to know is the one no letter can reach: no seat, no road, no name that would hold ink. So I use the only post we have ever shared — the book itself. If you read the margins as you made them, unasked, in the dark, after the honest work was done, you will read this. I have put it where a binder's hand does not go and a reader's eye does not think to look.

I will not ask who you are. You left that open in your own chapter, and I have come to believe the openness was a courtesy — the one soft thing you have done.

Here is what I ask instead; it is the only question I have left, and I have never once set it in a note: did you write before I gathered? I was forty years assembling this book. I chose the friar, paid the singer's passage, begged the skald, bribed the broadsheet-man; I thought, every year of it, that I was choosing. Then my copyists found your thread older than my quires, and your corrections older than the things they correct. So tell me plainly, who have never been anything but plain: did I compile this Compendium, or complete it? Was I its maker, or only its last errand?

I expect no answer. You have never answered anyone; you only correct. That is why I have written nothing here but a question — a question cannot be wrong, and leaves your pen no purchase. If silence is all you return, I will bind the silence in with the rest; I have printed less honest things.

I said once that yours was the only wholly honest thing between these covers, my own preface not excepted. This leaf is my attempt to make it two. I do not sign it. You, of all readers, know my hand.

Postscript, the same night. I chose this sheet myself from the Seat's own press: plain stock, held to the light before writing — a compiler's habit. Just now, folding it, I held it up again to see the fold true. The eye is in the paper. The same open eye my copyist found pressed into your last leaf — pressed at the paper's making. Before the question was written. Before, I begin to understand, it was asked. I have sat with it an hour. I am not taking another sheet. If the answer was in the paper before the question, then the question was well chosen. It stays.

Colophon. Unnumbered coda leaf, bound after Chapter XV and before the appendices. Voices per NARRATORS.md: the Curator, writing in his own person; the Veiled Hand, who does not appear and must not — the silence is the content, and no reply exists in canon or should be supplied. The open-eye watermark recurs from the closing note of Chapter XV (its first attestation); what may stand behind it is the matter of canon/secret-the-great-lie.md, which resolves it into no identity. [INVENTED]: the leaf entire — the letter, the postscript, and the watermark's recurrence on this sheet. And, this once, one line of colophon in the leaf's own hand: I certify nothing on this page except the paper, and I was wrong about the paper. — the C.

APPENDICES OF THE CURATOR

being tables, reckonings, and small necessary things the narrators could not be trusted to agree upon

The Curator

These pages are mine. The reader who has come this far deserves at least a few plain facts, arranged without poetry. — the Curator

Appendix A · The Reckoning of Years

All civilised dating counts from the birth of the Maelstrom: d.M., dopo il Maelstrom — "after the Maelstrom." Year 0 is the Great Fear (Grande Paura, in the old styling). (You will hear provincials expand d.M. as dopo Mithra — "after Mithra"; they are wrong, and the Church has given up correcting them.)

The ages, as the historians now divide them, with the old styling of each in parentheses:

AgeYears (d.M.)In brief
The Forgotten Times (I Tempi Dimenticati)before reckoningThe making; the Great Worms; the world before peoples' memory
The Ancient Days (I Giorni Antichi)before 0The reign of the Adepts; the Demon Wars; the Catastrophe
The Dark Days (I Giorni Oscuri)0 – ~1900Recovery; the rise of the Letian Empire; the Councils of the Peoples
The Burning Days (I Giorni Infuocati)~1900 – ~2590The Horde; the Young Kingdoms' secession; Saxul's fall
The New Days (I Giorni Nuovi)~2590 – ~3025The Second Council; the cascade of wars
The Age of the Tide (L'Era della Marea)~3025 – presentThe Tide (~3025–27) · the New Era of Chaos (3026–3260) · the New Equilibrium (3260 – now)

The present of this Compendium is ~3518 d.M. — two and a half centuries into the Equilibrium's calm. Distinguish three things the careless conflate: the Maelstrom (the storm itself, standing since year 0), the isolation (the seal upon the world that broke at the Tide), and the Age of the Tide (the age we live in, named for the Bewitched Tide that opened it). (The one who runs the world, and would set a table in some other year than mine, is directed to Appendix I.)

Appendix B · The Year of Ymir

One day is 24 hours (one dawn, eleven of day, one dusk, eleven of night). One month is 30 days; twelve months make one Cycle of 360 days. The months, with their seasons and birth-signs:

#MonthOld stylingSeasonThe sign's temper (bright / shadowed)
1GriffonGrifoneSpringbold, quick / rash, cutting
2BoarCinghialeSpringsteadfast / stubborn
3SalamanderSalamandraSpringclever, fluent / prying, shallow
4StagCervoSummergentle, wary / fearful, scheming
5WyvernVivernaSummergenerous, bright / vain, dogmatic
6UnicornUnicornoSummerexact, noble / anxious, cruel
7SerpentSerpenteAutumncharming / vain, sliding
8HawkFalcoAutumnfrank, far-seeing / reckless
9SpiderRagnoAutumnpatient, loyal / contrary
10ChimeraChimeraWinterquick-witted / aimless
11MagpieGazzaWintercurious, deft / grasping
12TortoiseTartarugaWinterwise, enduring / slow, timid

Of moons: Ishtar's silver moon keeps her courses as she always has. The red wanderer that troubled the sky from ~3026 receded from sight around 3260; the astronomers call it a comet, the Xebechani call it an eye, and I decline to arbitrate. (The reader of margins knows.)

Appendix C · Monies and Trade

Ymir has never kept one coin, and the reader should distrust any book that prices the world in a single currency. What the trader must know:

  • Cartosa & Meridian — struck doubloons and pieces-of-eight; letters of credit honoured in every honest port and several dishonest ones; the Blue Mantles tax magic like a cargo.
  • Armora & the Young Kingdoms — industrial marks and guild scrip; permits and licences are themselves a currency; never buy a Leyden jar second-hand.
  • Letia — church-minted coin under the Clericate; the tithe is not optional.
  • Helgedad — hacksilver, arm-rings, and the memory of who owes whom; coin is for foreigners.
  • Qi-Long — strung cash-coins, jade and silk for great sums; a sect's favour outbuys them all.
  • The Sadhir — salt tokens and the Sultanate's coral-standard; mana-salt for the discerning.
  • The Gaerwath — the elves trade in Arvo (powdered Essence) and, it is said, in bound Forces; do not trade there.
  • Between realms — weight of metal, Shald, and letters of credit; the portals move goods for those who can pay the tolls of the True Ways.

Appendix D · The Curator's Register of Persons

Every soul a narrator of mine names, and certain souls the histories name that my narrators do not. One dry line each: who they were, when they were it, and where in this book they walk. The reader who wants the stories has the chapter-numbers; the reader who wants more than stories has Chapter XIV·B, where the Church keeps a register of its own kind. Filed by the name the book most often uses, dynasts under their houses. A long dash (—) in the last place means no narrator of mine happens to name them. A dagger (†) means named only in hands I cannot account for, if your copy has them. Gods are Chapter II's business; dragons — Gwalgamaur the Golden, Ouroboros, Nihoggr and their kind — are beasts of Chapter XIV, and I bend my filing for no wing. Makers who survive only as possessive cases attached to famous objects are filed with their objects, in Appendix H.

Appendix E · Small Glossary of Terms the Narrators Assume

(Where an old-tongue form survives in older copies, it follows the term in italics.)

Adepts (Adepti) — the sorcerer-lords of the world before the Maelstrom; vanished. (See the margins, if your copy has them.) · Arvo — powdered Essence, the Gaerwath's currency and drug of power · Bewitched Tide (Marea Stregata) — the tide of wild magic that opened the present age · Channeler (Usufruitore) — any wielder of magic, in the law's cold word · Circles (Cerchie) — the six ranks by which demons are ordered; the Sovereigns stand beyond them · Crystal Seat (Seggio di Cristallo) — the Council of Peoples' hall at Elendor, where this book was bound · Essence (Essenza) — the raw stuff of magic; called mana by the vulgar · Flow (Flusso) — the divine realm of magic, the priests' channel · Maelstrom — the standing storm at the world's heart, over drowned Ragash · Marked (Marchiati) — those the Maelstrom marks in the womb · Mentalism (Mentalismo) — the mind's realm of magic · Nath — the three tiers of Names into which the Dark-Elf aristocracy (the Elar) is gathered · Relics / Magic Runes (Reliquie / Rune Magiche) — the six seals and the four sealed works of the Adepts, whose opening ended the old world's quiet · Sovereign Demons (Demoni Sovrani) — the great demons; most now dead; three walk · True Ways (Vere Vie) — the portal-roads, closed for an age and open again.

Appendix F · Of the Tongues of Ymir

The narrators of this book wrote in nine languages and assumed the reader kept all of them. The reader does not, and neither, in three cases, do I; what follows is what a compiler at Elendor can honestly certify, which is less than a grammar and more than nothing.

The tongueWhere it is spokenIts writingA note the reader may trust
Letian, and the Old ImperialLetia and every land Letia has held; the Clericate and the chanceries keep the elder registerthe imperial round-handThe "old styling" scattered through these appendices — dopo il Maelstrom, Grande Paura, the month-names — is the Old Imperial, as the Empire's charters have always written it. The daughter-speeches disagree with their mother chiefly about money.
CartosanCartosa, Meridian, and every port that owes themthe same letters, in a saltier handA Letian daughter fattened on sea-terms; the toponyms of the south — Punta del Toro, Santa Hermana — keep its music.
The Nortmaal speech, and NorsiHelgedad's marches; the Winter Forest keeps Norsi, which is olderrunes, cut rather than writtenA tongue of kennings: nothing is named that can be described sideways. Bargains sworn in it stay sworn, the grammar being witnessed.
The Qi-Long tonguesthe six kingdoms of the east, one speech apiece, mutually hostileone brush-script shared by all sixThe script is shared so that edicts may be read by the enemies they concern. Tonal; a bow is part of the grammar.
XebechaniXebech, Xuthal, and the toll-houses of the True Waysglyph-columns older than any warm alphabetUnchanged for millennia — a speech with no baby-talk, for a people who are grown, not raised.
The Elar tonguethe Gaerwatha script of ranksThe caste-words are its skeleton — Elar, Nemyel, Kelvar; Lyar, Nath, Gash — and there is no way to say you without declaring what the speaker may lawfully do to you.
Sarradhithe Sultanate of the Sadhira wheel-script, written in rings from the rim inwardThe trade-register is spoken through masks and admits no haggling; the desert does not bargain, and its language has caught the habit.
OphiritaOphiur; the Ivory Coalition coastlittle; the Thousand Songs are the archiveTonal praise-registers; a genealogy is a melody, and a library is a person who has learned it.
The Sohleugir trade-pidginthe wet markets of the southern seastide-marks, weights, and numeralsNo adjective survives translation into it, which its speakers account a feature. See the sounding-report at X·B.
The banner-speech of the Khanatesthe Belligerent KingdomsLetian letters, cut to orcish teethA tongue of tallies and banners; the chronicler Mugraash wrote a whole history in it, in a spelling that is somehow both wrong and vigorous.
The speech of the Little Folkthe Silver Islesthey write everyone's scripts and lend their own to no oneElendor's harbour speaks nine tongues before noon, and cheats politely in all of them.
The Adepts' tonguenowhere livinginscriptions on instruments of the elder ageScholarship reads perhaps forty words of it. Every one of them is a boast or a warning.

Of loan-words. Certain words travel with no passport, and the narrators use them unglossed: mana, the vulgar word for Essence, which every tongue owns and no tongue admits borrowing; Arvo, from the Elar; doubloon and pieces-of-eight, from the Cartosan counting-houses; drakkar, knarr, and dromen, from the Nortmaal shipwrights; Shald, which came out of the Arawak mountains with the glass it names; and d.M. itself, the Old Imperial abbreviation the whole world dates by, including the peoples who burned the Empire that coined it.

A short key to pronunciation, offered without warranty.

  • The Xebechani initial X is a sound the warm mouth approximates — something between sh and a held hiss; the Xebechani do not mind, which is worse. Say Xuthal "SHOO-thal" and Xochiyayotl "sho-chee-YAH-yotl" and you will be understood; say "Zanadu" for Xanadu, as the Letians do, and you will also be understood, which annoys no one but me.
  • Ssas'Kher: the doubled s is held; the mark is a swallowed breath. "SAHSS — KAIR," with a gulp between.
  • The eastern Qi- is "chee." The small marks over Qi-Long names are tones, not accents; do not attempt them in port.
  • Elar names: Lyar is "LEE-ar"; Celeblyar "keh-LEB-lee-ar"; Aelryn runs "ay-el" into one sound. Gaerwath is "GAIR-wath."
  • Sarradhi dh is a breathed d, as in the Letian the; Sadhir is "sa-DHEER."
  • In Nkishi, the N is its own syllable: "n-KEE-shee."
  • Hrafnkel: the H is not silent, and neither is anything else.
  • Tylweth Teg: "TUL-weth TEG," and smile while saying it; they will know why.
❧

[INVENTED]: essentially all linguistics — the phonology, the script-notes beyond the sources' bare word-lists, the pronunciation key entire, the wheel-script, the shared brush-script, and the identification of the book's "old styling" with the Old Imperial chancery-tongue (an editorial conceit, here made canon). The word-stock itself is canon throughout.

Appendix G · Of Herbs, Draughts, and Dusts

The narrators mention the road-pharmacy of Ymir in passing; the traveller deserves the list plain. Effects are given as the wise use them — the doses, and the prices of misuse, I leave to apothecaries and to conscience. (Bought honestly, half of these are medicine. Bought in an alley, all of them are stories that end badly.)

  • Utombe Distillate — distilled from a jungle leaf; erases the feeling of wounds for an hour (the wounds, regrettably, remain). In heavy doses a paralysing and sometimes killing poison.
  • Qarando Root — black-leaved; the Nkishi war-draught: euphoric fearlessness, at the cost of all caution. Warriors under it do not parry and do not chase; they only go forward.
  • Subotan — the violet poppy: bliss, torpor, waking dreams. Illegal in the Principality and available within sight of every courthouse in it.
  • Elin — a red alga; for a few racing moments the body outruns itself. Sailors chew it in storms and age accordingly.
  • Amatuba — spores of the deep fungi; brief, prodigious strength. Nkishi and Arawak warriors swear by it, and their healers swear at it.
  • Kirsemal — dried yellow flowers, inhaled: a profound stillness and clarity, prized by the Qi-adepts of the east; the body answers slowly while the spirit burns bright.
  • Xu Ran — a long dark leaf whose smoke steadies the mind for improvised sorcery.
  • Rud-Tekma — berries that sharpen a caster's art and sink the caster into trance; the entranced have been known to bless — or blast — whatever stands nearest.
  • Aljira — bluish liquor of Black Lotus nectar: restores a mage's spent power at once, and each dose is a wager with the body; lose, and it takes instead of gives.
  • Black Lotus — powdered petals; sorcery strengthened, every spell's grip lengthened. The vice of Ulan-Tang, where it is called an economy.
  • Green Lotus — of the Great Erg: a two-hour visionary coma, past and future shown to the prepared and riddles to everyone else — and each dose risks the sleeper's soul slipping its mooring into the Dream World, from which some do not come back for the body.
  • Juh'gad Draught — Gaerwath elf-alchemy, troll-gland and Moon-Wine: great strength yoked to a fearful, biddable spirit. They feed it to slaves at heavy labour. Everything one needs to know of the Gaerwath is in that sentence.

Appendix H · The Curator's Register of Instruments & Materials

The named things. One line each, and a last column the reader should read as I wrote it: not "where it is," which I rarely know, but where it was last credibly seen — credibly meaning I would lend the witness money. Chapter III promised that where the four Runes now stand "is matter for the historical chapters." The historical chapters, I find on re-reading them, never pay that debt; a register is where debts are settled, so I settle it below.

i · The Runes, and the six Relics that sealed them

The thingWhat it isLast credibly seen
The four Runes of Powerthe Adepts' four engines, one keyed to each realm of magic; the works the six Relics sealedWhere they have always stood: the vaults of Xanadu, in Xebechani keeping — unsealed these five centuries, and watched. The star-priests attest it to this day, and no one calls the star-priests liars twice.
Ignusa Relic; one of the six sealsXanadu, at the unsealing (~3025). No account since.
Saralisa RelicXanadu, at the unsealing. A Letian reliquary claims to hold it; the Clericate declines to open the box, which I note without comment.
Meletskar, called in the east the Masamunea Relic, and a blade; handled — with leave — by Sir Drusilde herself for one afternoon of 3027in the hand of Surya in the War of the Machines; the eastern ballads carry it home to the six kingdoms afterward, and ballads are the best witness I have.
Tassalunga RelicXanadu, at the unsealing. No account since.
Natharien, the Celestial Diadema Relic; a crown by shapeworn once in the Chaos years, the songs say, by a queen they will not name. No account since.
Oedringa RelicXanadu, at the unsealing. The dwarves say otherwise every solstice; the story improves annually, which is not what true stories do.

ii · Blades and instruments of name

The thingWhat it isLast credibly seen
Soul-Reaper (Mietianime)a sword; forged, the tale insists, by the death-god's own handat the side of Morannagul the Eternal, where it has hung for nine centuries. He is easy to find and hard to visit.
The Sword of Valdisthe blade of Valdis Nemertine, last heir of Letiathe field of the Broken Land, 2563. The Clericate maintains it was translated to Solanthya as a relic. The Clericate maintains.
Hellionone of the four elemental blades, of the firea fire-cult of the deep Erg is said to feed it; said by the sort of witness I would not lend money.
The Dark Avenger (Vendicatrice Oscura)an elemental blade, of the darktaken into the Gaerwath as tribute, the harbour-books of two ports swear; the Elar deny it with a completeness that persuades me of it.
Mornlossean elemental blade, of the icesold at Tallvar. Twice. By different liars.
Wave-Breaker (Frangionde)an elemental blade, of the water; Bulusture work of the Wars of the Wavesthe vault of the Sea Dragons at Santa Hermana, by their own registry — the one entry in this table backed by paperwork.
TessiondeWave-Breaker's twin, lostnowhere. This line is the register's one honest question, and I leave it standing open on purpose.
OblivionTofango's two-handed axe, forged at Hagelbarn by the alchemist Hans Schlecht on a commission whose name the Clericate has struck (the register of persons knows the entry); within it a mighty demon is imbued and trappedwith its bearer to the end, on the nameless peak where the hermit died. No one has since produced it, and I encourage no one to go looking.
The Crown of Sorcerya crown; of sorcery; the sources are confident of both words and of nothing elseno account. The register's honest blank.
In the Margin · the Veiled Hand

The Curator encourages no one to go looking for the axe. Correct. The axe does not need looking for. It is very good at being found.

iii · The Door of Despair, and its apparatus

The thingWhat it isLast credibly seen
The Door of Despaira sealed work of the elder world; no kin to the Runes, whatever the pamphlets spliceI do not print where it stands, chiefly because I do not know. Chapter III declined to write of it for soldiers; I decline for everyone. It remains sealed. That is the whole of my knowledge, and I am glad of the smallness of it.
The eight Forgotten Scrollsits apparatus, the first partscattered; eight originals and countless forgeries. The Crystal Seat holds two of the forgeries, purchased knowingly, to teach the difference.
The Key of Nothingits apparatus, the second partspoken of — as a thing present — in the depositions of the Ulan-Tang affair, 3026. The depositions are sealed. So, I am assured, is everything else.
The vessels of Elemental Bloodits apparatus, the third part; six vesselsRagash, the night of the Catastrophe, where the oldest accounts spend them. Whether spent is emptied, the accounts do not say.

iv · Materials the treatise omits

Sir Drusilde's chapter arms the reader with Shald, Orihalcum, Thalaras, Umbra, the two Steels, Black Powder, and Alchemical Coal (Chapter III, §VII). The trade knows seven more names. She would have wanted them measured; I can offer only what the markets whisper.

The materialWhat the trade says of itLast credibly seen
Lagoraka dull grey ore that drinks sound; mined, when it is mined at all, by the deaflining a counting-house strongroom in Armora, per its insurers.
Abyssal Glassblack glass said to be quenched in the Abyss itself; a scrying-piece of it shows the far side of whatever it is pointed ata masked factor's table in the Sadhir, where I am told it is used to check the weights. The weights are honest. Consider what that costs.
Bulusturemetal corrupted by elemental Water in the Wars of the Waves; never quite dry to the touchthe Wave-war arms above, and a suit of plate the Sea Dragons keep beside Wave-Breaker.
Galvorna black metal of elf-work, light as cloth and stubborn as sinthe Gaerwath does not export it. The Gaerwath has exported it exactly twice, which is how we know it exists.
Adamantinethe unarguable metal; its price is the location of the mine, which is nobody'sa hinge — one hinge — on a vault door at Naughrith, the dwarves' one public boast about it.
Eogthe grey sovereign of metals, worked only by arts now lost; elder-age pieces circulate and are not re-forged, because they cannot bean heirloom blade-core auctioned at Meridian in 3499; the buyer is not recorded, the price is, and I declined to believe it until I saw the ledger.
Yarhim-shellshell of the Yarhim — whatever a Yarhim is; the shell is attested, the beast is notthe shell: an Ivory Coalition curiosity-house at Zabhula. The beast: a matter I have referred to the huntsman of Chapter XIV, who wrote back one word — "downwind."

Of the lesser wonders — the named armours, the sceptres, the luck-charms of Gwynder the Unlucky, the hundred titled books that circulate with opinions of their own — the catalogue is a book in itself, and in fact several; the makers (Kellar, Droan, Tshot, Urkhramest the Devout, and their kind) survive chiefly as possessive cases, and I have let them rest there.

Appendix I · Doors into Ymir (GM only)

For the Game Master alone

GM ONLY. This appendix, like the fifteenth chapter, is for the one who runs the world, and for no other eyes. Players: Appendix H was your last stop; Appendix J is your next.

In the same hand as the margins, found — the Curator attests — already bound.

The Curator fixed this book's camera at 3518 and nowhere says the tripod moves. It moves. The line from the Great Fear to this binding is three and a half thousand years deep, and the deep is usable. Here are five doors on that line. For each I give you the four things a table actually needs: who reigns; what exists yet; what is commonly known against what is not yet true; and which leaves of this book exist — because a book is also a thing in the world, and most of this one has not been written yet, wherever you choose to stand.

The first door · The Burning Days (~1900–2590). Set your year anywhere in the long scourge; if you want a single hinge, take 2563, the year of the Broken Land. Who reigns: an Empire with a living crown — Letia has an heir until the day Valdis Nemertine spends herself on Saxul; the Khans squabble on the bones of the captive east after 2030; Cartosa is a young Principality (princes from 1906); the Qi-Long's six kingdoms are raw and their Dragon-Gods newly in residence; from 2550 the Gaerwath has one master, and he is not going anywhere. What exists: the Coalition of Peoples, as parchment (1735); the Blue Mantles' Academy only after 2508; no Crystal Seat (2590), no Church-rule in Letia (2610), no Armorite schism, no Red Book. The world is sealed: portals are dead stone, teleportation is a scholar's embarrassment, and everything travels by sail. Known, and not yet true: everyone knows demons are real, historical, and beaten — two Sovereigns slain is the age's pride. No one living has seen a working gate. "Xanadu" is an eastern rumour; the six Relics are six unrelated treasures in six unrelated stories; the word tide means water. Which leaves exist: none. Chapter I's account was old before any date on this page, but the book is thirty lifetimes off; the friar's chronicle, the sailor's diary, the arcanist's treatise are unwritten; their sources are alive, and quarrelling. Play here for war with banners on it — horde, crusade, and a crown worth dying for, in a world where the doors do not open.

The second door · The eve of the Tide (3015–3025). The very years the old campaigns were played in; the storm is loaded and nobody has fired it. Who reigns: the High Theocrat at Solanthya; Leonius VonGryffen in Armora, calling the Theocrat corrupt a little louder each year; in Cartosa, Rodriguez XIII until the Black Sun year, then Alberto V (3017); Morannagul; the Eternal Pharaoh; six Dragon-Gods. What exists: everything of the New Days — Crystal Seat, Blue Mantles, Sea Dragons, church-rule — and none of the age to come: gates still dead, red moon unrisen, the S.C.M. unfounded, the Red Book unwritten. The wars cascade: Wolves from 3015, Waves 3018–23, Machines from 3025, and Berthrant Vaelaer is in Helgedad with thirteen thousand five hundred, scouring. Known, and not yet true: everyone knows the wars; no one knows they are a fuse. A respected inquisitor of Mithra is quietly curdling toward Ulan-Tang, and his name is still on the rolls. The six Relics are antiquarians' gossip. Which leaves exist: still none. Drusilde is alive, mid-career, two years from her treatise; the Crier's presses print his grandfather's numbers; the skald's Wolves-lay is being lived, not sung; Ramiro is five centuries unborn. Play here to stand in the last quiet and know, as your players will, exactly what the quiet is for.

The third door · The Tide itself (3025–3027). Two years in which everything true becomes false in order. The Relics are gathered; the Runes unsealed at Xanadu; the bell does not crack, it ceases; every gate on Ymir lights in the same hour; the Bewitched Tide rolls out of the Maelstrom; the Isle-of-Death barrier falls; the prison cracks, the continent rises, and three Sovereigns walk ashore. In 3026 the struck-off inquisitor opens Ulan-Tang and the red moon rises; Ouroboros wakes and Alfheim burns in a season; Leonius's schism goes from pulpit to powder. Who reigns: whoever can hold a balcony. What exists: by 3027, the Red Book — dated Era of the Tide 2 — and Armora's S.C.M., invented in a hurry, for reasons. Known, and not yet true: here the ground of the appendix inverts — in these years almost nothing is commonly known and everything is true. The world at large knows quakes, strange tides, a wrong moon, and dead men walking; the causal chain — Relics, Runes, bell — is known to perhaps a dozen souls on Ymir. Your players may be among them, which is the whole offer of this door. Which leaves exist: one. Chapter III is wet ink in Armora, and its author is correcting proofs while the sky is wrong.

The fourth door · The New Era of Chaos (3026–3260). Two centuries and a third with the red moon overhead, the doors open, and the dead impolite. Who reigns: the Church holds the north like a dyke; Vespertina VonGryffen makes her peace with Letia against the Khans, and her line keeps Armora; Ugrumuulsh One-Eye and his successors ride the east; the Tanoth take Hagelbarn back; the deep dwarves seal themselves under the White Mountains and change; part of Xebech is simply elsewhere for a while, and does not explain itself when it returns. What exists: gates, working and feared; the demon-continent, on the charts and shunned; every institution of the bright chapters, but younger, harder, and armed. Known, and not yet true: the moon is ordinary — children are born and die under it; that it is an eye is known to the Xebechani and believed by no one else. The Crier's golden age is being printed in these years too — as propaganda about the future, numbers no living subscriber will see; the skald's matter is fresh grief. Drusilde's treatise rides in soldiers' satchels. Which leaves exist: III, and the songs that will become XII·B are already being kept. Play here for the world your Equilibrium-era players' grandmothers survived: grimdark, open-doored, and lit from above by something that has not blinked.

The fifth door · The New Equilibrium (~3518). The default; the year the Curator's camera stands on. Who reigns: Serafina VonGryffen II, the Magnificent, in Armora; the High Theocrat at Solanthya; the Carrillo still, in Cartosa; Morannagul, in his nine hundred and sixty-eighth regnal year; the Council of Peoples at Elendor, which is the nearest thing the world has to a roof. What exists: all of it; that is what a calm is. The red moon receded in 3260. Known, and not yet true: the common knowledge is the bright text of Chapters I through XIV, entire — that is what those chapters are. What is not common knowledge is every margin in this book, plus one measurement: the Sohleugir report the Maelstrom's rhythm faltering, and the Sohleugir do not exaggerate. Which leaves exist: the book in your hands, being copied at Elendor while you read it. Play here for the long exhale — and remember, before you let the calm feel safe, whose breath it is that is being held.

Five doors. The fifteenth chapter told you what the house is; the Workbook after it stocks the rooms. This page is only the keyring. Do not lose it, Curator's guest — the Curator does not know he is carrying it.

Appendix J · Of the Plates, and an Index of Places

Beside this Compendium, on the east wall of the copying-hall, hangs the great geographical map of 3518 — the one the fifth chapter's soundings underlie, from which every modern chart descends. A reduced engraving has been subscribed for, so that copies of this book need not travel with a wall; the engraver, however, is a craftsman, and craftsmen have their own calendar. Until the plates are cut, their descriptions must serve. I have checked each against the wall.

a · The plates, described

  • Plate the First — The Ring of the World. Ymir entire, a globe flattened by honest violence: one Central Ocean, the lands set round it like teeth in a jaw, and at the dead centre the Maelstrom, which the engraver is instructed to render as the sailors see it — a wall, not a whirl. The northern margin is banded the Frozen Lands, the southern the Obsidian Lands; the scale-bar is two thousand kilometres, and the lost day of the circumnavigation is cited in the cartouche as proof of the globe.
  • Plate the Second — The Sacred North. Letia of the marches and baronies; Solanthya gilded at its heart (the label, on older charts, standing for the whole Empire); the White Mountains with Naughrith cut into them; eastward, fading deliberately at the edge, the captive marches the Khans hold — the Belligerent Kingdoms, drawn from Letian survey and orcish sufferance.
  • Plate the Third — The Frozen Isle. Helgedad in its six old marches; the Wall of Aslund riding the Kelmark cliffs for four hundred kilometres; the Golden Halls and Stonebridge under their mountains; the Winter Forest; Nortmaar of the clans; Harbor under the Shining Tower.
  • Plate the Fourth — The Steam-Coast. The Young Kingdoms: Armora with its seven districts inset at large scale (the fog is not drawn; the fog is understood); Wald, Zaalesha, Vallanya, Caeldir, Tydriell; the airship-roads marked in dotted optimism.
  • Plate the Fifth — The Southern Seas. Cartosa and Meridian, twin islands and rival flags; the Sierra Plata and Sierra Grande; the Twin Coasts; the ports from Punta del Toro to Santa Hermana; the drowned ground off Costa Sileña marked with the chartmaker's politest hatching.
  • Plate the Sixth — The Sands. The Great Erg, with Sathe the caravan-port at its sea-gate; Ulan-Tang on the river Tang; Khorish of the Eternal Pharaohs; and south across the plate's fold the Sadhir, the Shimmering Desert, drawn white on white — the engraver protests, and is overruled; the desert is like that.
  • Plate the Seventh — The Morning Country. Ophiur: the Ivory Coalition coast — Zabhula, Akhon, Ga'Namesh; ruined Gazal at the feet of the Dark Mountains; Horatli under Mount Horat; the savanna of Tarkur, across which the engraver is instructed to letter, in small capitals, THE INTERIOR TRADES IN YOU.
  • Plate the Eighth — The East. The six kingdoms of the Qi-Long, each in its banner-colour, with Haiguang and the old Capital of Light; south of them Xebech, where Xuthal is marked with the cartographer's one traditional joke — position as at the drawing — and Xanadu is marked without one; Loquitchatzotech edged in black, as is the custom for coasts with no birds.
  • Plate the Ninth — The Elvish South-East. Alfheim, the new city built beside its own ruin at Ost-en-Galad; the Gaerwath ring, ten islands drawn from soundings taken at forty leagues' respectful distance; the Silver Isles, with Elendor and the Crystal Seat — where the reader, so to speak, is standing.
  • Plate the Tenth — The Shunned and the Veiled. Kyria, drawn as its fog, the island beneath taken on trust; the Isle of Demons, a coastline only, the soundings stopping where the birds did; and the Maelstrom's wall once more, at the largest scale of all, with drowned Ragash beneath it marked in the manner of a grave.

c · Names for which I hold no account

The wall-map is more honest than its keeper would like. It carries labels in the engraver's best hand for which no narrator of mine — in fifteen chapters, seven late leaves, and a great deal of correspondence — has ever supplied one line of account. I will not invent what I do not know, and I will not quietly omit what the map plainly shows. Here they are, exactly as lettered:

Itza · U-aj-tanis · Hibernia · Ljone del Saos · Luveburk · Cariba — scattered on the ring's western and northern reaches — and Tema-li · Ost-en-Mano · Dalkis · Thulos, which the map sets on the southern continent's inland distances, beyond where the coastal narrators turn back.

Ten names; ten blank pages. If your table has been to any of them, it knows more than the Crystal Seat does, and the account is yours to write. I ask only this: date it.

In the Margin · the Veiled Hand

A blank page is an invitation. So is an unlocked door. The Curator means the first kind. Mean both.

Colophon (Appendix J). Plates, index, and the unaccounted names, by the Curator. Drawn from canon/geography.md (the regions; the world-map labels with no prose — kept as frontier per GEO-4; the Frozen/Obsidian Lands frame and the 2000 km scale; the ten Gaerwath isles), sources/maps/ (the 3518 geographical map, canonical per GEO-3; the globe per GEO-13), and the chapters as bound (the index compiled against I–XV and XII·B; later leaves deferred to a second impression). [INVENTED]: the plate-partition and every plate-description (the map is canon; its division into ten plates, the engraver, the subscription, and the cartouche-jokes are mine); the margin is a deliberate open GM hook. The ten unaccounted labels are canon map-text and deliberately left blank (GEO-4 = frontier).

Appendix K · Of This Book's Making (out-of-world note)

The Compendium is the player-facing world bible of Ymir. The body text of every chapter is an in-world document with an in-world author's bias; the ⟡ margins ⟡ are for the Game Master only and carry the campaign's hidden truths. In its present binding the book comprises the front matter (with the contents page, "The Order of This Book"), Chapters I–XV with their late leaves (IX·B, X·B, X·C, XII·B, XII·C, XII·D, XIV·B, XV·B), two unnumbered leaves (the censored facsimile after Chapter VI, and the closing note), and eleven appendices, A through K — of which Appendix I, like Chapter XV and its Workbook, is GM-only. The narrators are inventions; the world they describe is drawn from the canon files in canon/ (which cite the original source documents), with connective inventions flagged chapter by chapter — and appendix by appendix — in each colophon. The register of narrators lives in NARRATORS.md; the full lore-reference and its sources live beside this manual in the repository. Contradictions between narrators are deliberate where the sources themselves disagreed — the decisions that reconciled them are logged in conflicts.md.

Colophon. Appendices A–C, E, G, and K by the Curator (framing voice). Drawn from canon/calendar.md, canon/history.md, canon/economy.md, canon/cosmology.md, canon/magic.md (Appendix G: the substances of sources/raw/Additions.md), and the decisions log in conflicts.md (HIS-1, META-2, META-5, COS-6/13, COS-22). Appendices D, F, H, I, and J carry their own colophons above. Re-lettering note: the glossary (formerly D) is now E; the herbs (formerly E) are now G; this note (formerly F) is now K.
